Furuat al-Qawaid — Derived Applications
intermediate
10 min
Introduction to the Maxim and Concessions in Hajj, Clothing, and Sales
Listing concessions based on the maxim of hardship brings ease

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the maxim 'al-mashaqqah tajlib al-taysir' and apply it to identify the basis for Hanafi concessions in ihram, silk, salam, and options.

Core Idea
Hardship necessitates ease: concessions depart from strict qiyas to prevent undue difficulty.

The Hanafi school extensively uses the maxim 'hardship brings ease' to permit exceptions from general rulings. This lesson explores early examples from the text: exiting ihram when prevented, wearing silk for itching, salam sales, and buyer's options. Each is justified by the need to remove hardship.

Guided Path
1
Identify the maxim
Recognize that the passage lists applications of 'al-mashaqqah tajlib al-taysir'. Look for keywords like 'إباحة' or 'جوز'.
The maxim ties all concessions together.
2
For each concession, note the normal ruling
E.g., silk is normally haram for men; ihram normally cannot be exited. Each concession departs from the original.
Contrast the default with the exception.
3
Identify the hardship avoided
E.g., hardship of staying in ihram when unable, hardship of itch without silk, hardship of poverty without salam.
The hardship is the reason for the concession.
4
Classify the legal effect
Is it a permissibility (ibaha), a right (khiyar), or a validity (sihha)?
Consequences vary: some make acts permissible, some give an option.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كذلك، وإباحة التحليل من الحج بالإحصار والفوات وإباحة أبي يوسف رحمه الله رعي حشيش الحرم للحاج في الموسم تيسيرًا، ولبس الحرير للحكة والقتال وبيع الموصوف في الذمة كالسلم جوز على خلاف القياس دفعا لحاجة المفاليس والاكتفاء برؤية طاهر الصبرة والأنموذج ومشروعية خيار الشرط للمشتري دفعا للندم وخيار نقد الثمن دفعًا للمماطلة. ومن هذا القبيل بيع الأمانة المسمى ببيع جوزه مشایخ بلخ وبخارى توسعة وبيانه في شرح الكنز من باب خيار الشرط. ومن ذلك أفتى المتأخرون بالرد لخيار الغبن الفاحش ؛ إما مطلقا أو إذا كان فيه غرور رحمة على المشتري.
الوفاء ؛
ومنه الرد بالعيب والتحالف والإقالة والحوالة والرهن والضمان والإبراء والقرض والشركة والصلح والحجر والوكالة والإجارة والمزارعة والمساقاة، على قولهما المفتى به للحاجة، والمضاربة والعارية والوديعة، للمشقة العظيمة في أن كل واحد لا ينتفع إلا بما هو ملكه ولا يستوفي إلا ممَّن عليه حقه ولا يأخذه إلا بكماله، ولا يتعاطى أموره إلا بنفسه فسهل الأمر بإباحة الانتفاع بملك الغير بطريق الإجارة والإعارة والقرض وبالاستعانة بالغير وكالة وإبداعًا وشركة ومضاربة ومساقاة، وبالاستيفاء من غير المديون حوالة وبالتوثيق على الدين برهن وكفيل، ولو بالنفس وبإسقاط بعض الدين صلحا أو كله إبراء ولحاجة افتداء يمينه ؛ جوزنا الصلح عن إنكار ولفقد ما شرعت الإجارة له لو جعلت المنافع أُجرة عند اتحاد الجنس قلنا لا يجوز، وقلنا الإجارة على منفعة غير مقصودة من العين لا تجوز للاستغناء عنها بالعارية كما علم في إجارة البزازية.
،
ومن التخفيف جواز العقود الجائزة، لأن لزومها شاق فتكون سببًا لعدم تعاطيها، ولزوم اللازمة وإلا لم يستقر بيع ولا غيره ووقفنا عزل الوكيل على علمه دفعًا للحرج عنه، وكذا عزل القاضي وصاحب وظيفته.
ومنه إباحة الفطر للطبيب والشاهد، وعند الخطبة وللسيد. ومنه جواز النكاح من غير نظر لما في اشتراطه من المشقة التي لا يتحملها كثير من الناس في بناتهم وأخواتهم ؛ من نظر كل خاطب فناسب التيسير فلم يكن فيه خيار رؤية بخلاف البيع فإنه يصح قبل الرؤية وله الخيار لعدم المشقة، ومن ثم قلنا إن الأمر إيجاب في النكاح بخلاف البيع، ومن هنا وسع فيه أبو حنيفة رحمه الله فجوَّزه بلا ولي ومن غير اشتراط عدالة الشهود، ولم يفسده بالشروط المفسدة، ولم يخصه بلفظ النكاح والتزويج بل قال ينعقد بما يفيد ملك العين للحال، وصححه بحضور ابني العاقدين وناعسين وسكارى يذكرونه بعد الصحو، وبعبارة النساء، وجوّز شهادتهنَّ فيه، فانعقد بحضرة رجل وامرأتين كل ذلك دفعا لمشقة الزنا وما يترتب عليه. ومن هنا قيل عجبت لحنفي يزني. ومنه إباحة أربع نسوة؛ فلم يقتصر على واحدة تيسيرًا على الرجل وعلى النساء أيضًا لكثرتهنَّ، ولم يزد على أربعة لما فيه من المشقة على الرجل في القسم وغيره. ومنه مشروعية الطلاق لما في البقاء على الزوجية من المشقة عند التنافر، وكذا مشروعية الخلع والافتداء والرجعة في العدة قبل الثلاث، ولم يشرع دائما لما فيه من المشقة على الزوجة . ومنه وقوع الطلاق على المولى بمضي أربعة أشهر دفعا للضرر عنها.
ومنه مشروعية الكفَّارة في الظهار واليمين تيسيرًا على المكلفين، وكذا التخيير في كفَّارة اليمين لتكررها بخلاف بقية الكفَّارات لندرة وقوعها، ومشروعية التخيير في نذر معلق بشرط لا يُراد كونه بين كفَّارة اليمين والوفاء بالمنذور على ما عليه الفتوى. وإليه رجع الإمام قبل موته بسبعة أيام.
ومنه مشروعية الكتابة ليتخلص العبد من دوام الرقّ لما فيه من العسر، ولم يبطلها بالشروط الفاسدة توسعة.
ومنه مشروعية الوصية عند الموت ليتدارك الإنسان ما فرط منه في حال حياته وصح له في الثلث دون ما زاد عليه دفعًا لضرر الورثة حتى أجزناها بالجميع عند عدم الوارث، وأوقفناها على إجازة بقية الورثة إذا كانت لوارث وأبقينا التركة على ملك الميت حكمًا حتى تقضى حوائجه منها رحمة عليه، ووسعنا الأمر في الوصية فجوزناها بالمعدوم ولم نبطلها بالشروط الفاسدة.
·
ومنه إسقاط الإثم عن المجتهدين في الخطأ والتيسير عليهم بالاكتفاء بالظن ولو كلفوا الأخذ باليقين لشقّ وعسر الوصول إليه، ووسع أبو حنيفة رحمه الله في باب القضاء والشهادات تيسيرًا؛ فصحح تولية الفاسق وقال إن فسقه لا يعزله وإنما يستحقه، ولم يوجب تزكية الشهود حلاً لحال المسلمين على الصلاح، ولم يقبل الجرح المجرَّد في الشاهد ووسع أبو يوسف رحمه الله في القضاء والوقف. والفتوى على قوله فيما يتعلق بهما، وجوز للقاضي تلقين الشاهد وجوز كتاب القاضي إلى القاضي من غير سفر ولم يشترط فيه شيئًا مما شرطه الإمام، وصحح الوقف على النفس وعلى جهة تنقطع، ووقف المشاع ولم يشترط التسليم إلى المتولي ولا حكم
Similarly, the permissibility of exiting ihram in Hajj due to restraint (ihsar) and missing (fawat), and the permissibility according to Abu Yusuf (may Allah have mercy on him) of grazing the herbage of the Haram for a pilgrim during the season as ease, and wearing silk for itching and fighting, and selling a described item in the dhimmah like salam (advance payment) was permitted contrary to analogy to fulfill the need of the destitute, and sufficiency with seeing the visible part of a heap and a sample, and legislation of option (khiyar al-shart) for the buyer to prevent regret, and option of paying the price to prevent procrastination. Of this kind is the sale of trust (bay' al-amanah) called bay' ... by the scholars of Balkh and Bukhara as expansion, and its explanation is in Sharh al-Kanz from the chapter of khiyar al-shart. From that, the later jurists gave fatwa of return for the option of gross fraud (khiyar al-ghubn al-fahish), either absolutely or if there is deception, as mercy on the buyer.
Fulfillment (al-wafa'): And from it is the return due to defect, mutual oaths (tahlif), rescission (iqalah), transfer of debt (hawalah), pledge (rahn), guarantee (daman), release (ibra'), loan (qard), partnership (shirkah), compromise (sulh), interdiction (hajr), agency (wakalah), lease (ijarah), sharecropping (muzara'ah), and irrigation contract (musaqah), according to the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) with the fatwa given for need, and mudarabah, ariyah (loan of benefit), and wadi'ah (deposit), due to the great hardship that each one does not benefit except from what is his property, and does not receive except from the one upon whom his right is due, and does not take it except in full, and does not conduct his affairs except by himself. So the matter was eased by permitting benefit from another's property by way of lease, loan, and loan; and seeking assistance from another through agency, deposit, partnership, mudarabah, and musaqah; and taking from someone other than the debtor through hawalah; and securing the debt by pledge and surety, even by oneself; and dropping part of the debt through compromise or all through release, and for the need of redeeming his oath; we permitted compromise in case of denial, and due to the lack of that for which lease was legislated if benefits were made the rent when the type is the same, we said it is not permissible, and we said lease for a benefit not intended from the asset is not permissible due to dispensing with it through ariyah as known in the lease of bazaziyah.
And from the alleviations: the permissibility of non-binding contracts, because their binding would be difficult and thus cause them to be avoided, and the binding of binding contracts otherwise no sale or other would be stable, and we made the dismissal of an agent conditional upon his knowledge to prevent hardship upon him, and similarly the dismissal of a judge and the holder of his office.
And from it is the permissibility of breaking fast for a doctor and a witness, and during the sermon (khutbah), and for a master. And from it is the permissibility of marriage without seeing [the prospective spouse] because the hardship of requiring it, which many people cannot bear for their daughters and sisters—each suitor seeing—so ease was appropriate, so there is no option of seeing (khiyar al-ru'yah) in it, unlike sale, for it is valid before sight and has the option due to lack of hardship. Hence we said that the command is obligatory in marriage unlike sale, and hence Abu Hanifa (may Allah have mercy on him) was lenient and permitted it without a guardian and without requiring the justice of witnesses, and did not invalidate it by invalid conditions, and did not restrict it to the wording of nikah or tazwij, but said it is concluded by anything that indicates ownership of the object immediately, and validated it with the presence of the sons of the two contractors, drowsy and drunk persons who remember after sobriety, and by women's words, and permitted their testimony in it, so it is concluded in the presence of one man and two women, all that to prevent the hardship of adultery and its consequences. Hence it was said: 'I wonder at a Hanafi who commits adultery.' And from it is the permissibility of four wives; he did not restrict to one as ease for the man and also for women due to their abundance, and did not exceed four due to the hardship upon the man in division and other matters. And from it is the legislation of divorce due to the hardship of remaining in marriage when there is discord, and similarly legislation of khul', fidya, and return (raj'ah) in the waiting period before the third pronouncement, and it was not made perpetual due to the hardship upon the wife. And from it is the occurrence of divorce upon a husband who took an oath (moli) by the passage of four months to prevent harm upon her.
And from it is the legislation of expiation in zihar and oaths as ease for the obligated persons, and similarly the choice in expiation for an oath due to its frequency unlike other expiations due to their rarity, and the legislation of choice in a suspended vow with a condition not intended between the expiation of an oath and fulfilling the vowed act, according to what the fatwa is upon. And the Imam returned to it seven days before his death.
And from it is the legislation of kitabah (contract of manumission) so that the slave may be freed from continuous slavery due to the hardship in it, and it was not invalidated by invalid conditions as expansion.
And from it is the legislation of bequest at death so that one may make up for what he neglected during his life, and it is valid in one-third and not more to prevent harm to the heirs, so we permitted it with the whole when there is no heir, and we made it conditional upon the permission of the remaining heirs if it is for an heir, and we kept the estate on the deceased's ownership legally until his needs are fulfilled from it as mercy upon him, and we expanded the matter in bequest by permitting it for a non-existent [thing] and not invalidating it by invalid conditions.
And from it is the removal of sin from mujtahids in error and easing upon them by sufficing with probability; if they were required to take certainty, it would be difficult and hard to reach. And Abu Hanifa (may Allah have mercy on him) was lenient in the chapter of judgment and testimonies as ease; he validated the appointment of a corrupt person and said his corruption does not remove him [from office] but rather he deserves it, and he did not require the verification of witnesses' integrity as a solution for the state of Muslims as being virtuous, and did not accept abstract assault (jarh mujarrad) against a witness. And Abu Yusuf (may Allah have mercy on him) was lenient in judgment and endowment; the fatwa is upon his statement regarding them. He permitted the judge to prompt a witness, permitted the judge's letter to another judge without travel and did not require in it any of what the Imam required, validated a wqf upon oneself and upon a terminating destination, and validated a wqf of undivided property without requiring delivery to the trustee nor a ruling.
Source pages p. 68

Commentary
This passage is a detailed enumeration of Hanafi concessions derived from the overarching legal maxim 'hardship brings ease' (al-mashaqqah tajlib al-taysir). The author, likely Ibn Nujaym or a commentator on al-Ashbah wa al-Naza'ir, systematically lists applications across various chapters of fiqh. Each example illustrates how a ruling that would normally be based on strict analogy (qiyas) is relaxed due to hardship, need, or custom.

The passage begins with Hajj-related concessions: permitting exit from ihram due to restraint or missing the standing, and Abu Yusuf's opinion allowing grazing in the Haram for pilgrims. Then it moves to other concessions: wearing silk for medical or combat reasons, salam sales, option clauses, and the sale of trust (bay' al-amanah) as practiced by the scholars of Balkh and Bukhara. The 'option of gross fraud' (khiyar al-ghubn al-fahish) is mentioned as a later fatwa.

The central section discusses contracts like ijarah, ariyah, qard, wakalah, etc., which are normally based on strict property rights but are permitted due to the great hardship of doing everything oneself. The author explains the reasoning: ease is granted by allowing benefit from another's property through various contracts, and by allowing collection from third parties via hawalah, securing with pledge and surety, etc.

Further concessions: non-binding contracts (like wakalah, shirkah) are kept non-binding because binding would lead to avoidance; the dismissal of an agent requires knowledge to prevent hardship; judges and officials are treated similarly. Fasting is broken for a doctor, witness, during sermon, and master. Marriage is permitted without prior sight of the spouse (no option of sight), unlike sale, due to the hardship of requiring all suitors to see; Abu Hanifa went further by allowing marriage without guardian, without requiring witness justice, with imperfect wording, even with intoxicated parties, and with women's testimony, all to prevent the greater hardship of adultery. Polygyny is permitted up to four as ease, but not more due to hardship on the husband. Divorce, khul', and raj'ah are legislated due to hardship of staying in discord; a husband who swears to abstain (ila) is divorced automatically after four months to protect the wife.

Expiation (kaffarah) is legislated for zihar and oaths as ease, and choice in oath expiation is given due to frequency. Similar choice is given in suspended vows. Kitabah (manumission contract) is permitted to free the slave from perpetual servitude. Bequests are permitted to make up for missed acts, limited to one-third to protect heirs, but can be whole if no heir, and may be conditional upon heir's permission. Bequest for a non-existent thing (like building a mosque before construction) is allowed.

Finally, the passage addresses ijtihad: mujtahids are excused for error, sufficing with probability. In judiciary, Abu Hanifa allowed appointing a corrupt person and did not require witnesses' integrity to be verified; Abu Yusuf's leniency in judgment and waqf became the fatwa. He allowed the judge to prompt a witness, and the judge's letter to another judge without travel, and validated waqf on self and on a terminating category, and waqf of undivided property without delivery.

Throughout, the author emphasizes that these are all instances of the principle of easing hardship, and the Fatwa is often given on the more lenient opinion.

Key Terms
المشقة تجلب التيسير (al-mashaqqah tajlib al-taysir): A major legal maxim meaning that when a ruling causes hardship, the law provides ease through concessions.
خيار الغبن الفاحش (khiyar al-ghubn al-fahish): Option to rescind a sale due to gross disparity in price, where the seller took advantage of the buyer.
تيسير (taysir): Ease or facilitation, the basis for concessions in rulings.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why was salam sale permitted despite being contrary to analogy?
A) Because it is explicitly mentioned in the Quran.
B) To fulfill the need of the destitute.
C) Because it was the practice of the people of Medina.
D) To avoid the hardship of finding a buyer.

Key Takeaway
The maxim 'hardship brings ease' justifies departures from strict analogy in Hajj, clothing, and sales.

Furuat al-Qawaid — Derived Applications
intermediate
8 min
Concessions in Contracts and Transactions
Listing contract concessions based on the maxim

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain how the maxim 'hardship brings ease' permits various contracts like lease, loan, and agency, which would otherwise be invalid due to strict ownership rules.

Core Idea
Need permits contracts that allow using others' property, avoiding the hardship of self-sufficiency.

The passage highlights a wide range of contracts permitted to ease transactions. It argues that requiring each person to own what they need would cause great hardship, so the law permits leases, loans, partnerships, agency, etc. The reasoning is that these contracts allow benefit from another's property and delegation of tasks.

Guided Path
1
Identify the problem
The default rule is that one can only benefit from one's own property. This would be extremely difficult.
2
List the contracts permitted as ease
Examples: ijarah, ariyah, qard, wakalah, shirkah, mudarabah, etc.
The text gives a long list.
3
Understand the reasoning
These contracts allow using others' property or services, easing the burden of acquiring everything oneself.
The author explains the reasoning in detail.
4
Note which positions are mufta bihi
Many are according to the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) and are adopted as fatwa.

Source Text

كذلك، وإباحة التحليل من الحج بالإحصار والفوات وإباحة أبي يوسف رحمه الله رعي حشيش الحرم للحاج في الموسم تيسيرًا، ولبس الحرير للحكة والقتال وبيع الموصوف في الذمة كالسلم جوز على خلاف القياس دفعا لحاجة المفاليس والاكتفاء برؤية طاهر الصبرة والأنموذج ومشروعية خيار الشرط للمشتري دفعا للندم وخيار نقد الثمن دفعًا للمماطلة. ومن هذا القبيل بيع الأمانة المسمى ببيع جوزه مشایخ بلخ وبخارى توسعة وبيانه في شرح الكنز من باب خيار الشرط. ومن ذلك أفتى المتأخرون بالرد لخيار الغبن الفاحش ؛ إما مطلقا أو إذا كان فيه غرور رحمة على المشتري.

ومنه مشروعية الكفَّارة في الظهار واليمين تيسيرًا على المكلفين، وكذا التخيير في كفَّارة اليمين لتكررها بخلاف بقية الكفَّارات لندرة وقوعها، ومشروعية التخيير في نذر معلق بشرط لا يُراد كونه بين كفَّارة اليمين والوفاء بالمنذور على ما عليه الفتوى. وإليه رجع الإمام قبل موته بسبعة أيام.
ومنه مشروعية الكتابة ليتخلص العبد من دوام الرقّ لما فيه من العسر، ولم يبطلها بالشروط الفاسدة توسعة.
ومنه مشروعية الوصية عند الموت ليتدارك الإنسان ما فرط منه في حال حياته وصح له في الثلث دون ما زاد عليه دفعًا لضرر الورثة حتى أجزناها بالجميع عند عدم الوارث، وأوقفناها على إجازة بقية الورثة إذا كانت لوارث وأبقينا التركة على ملك الميت حكمًا حتى تقضى حوائجه منها رحمة عليه، ووسعنا الأمر في الوصية فجوزناها بالمعدوم ولم نبطلها بالشروط الفاسدة.
·
ومنه إسقاط الإثم عن المجتهدين في الخطأ والتيسير عليهم بالاكتفاء بالظن ولو كلفوا الأخذ باليقين لشقّ وعسر الوصول إليه، ووسع أبو حنيفة رحمه الله في باب القضاء والشهادات تيسيرًا؛ فصحح تولية الفاسق وقال إن فسقه لا يعزله وإنما يستحقه، ولم يوجب تزكية الشهود حلاً لحال المسلمين على الصلاح، ولم يقبل الجرح المجرَّد في الشاهد ووسع أبو يوسف رحمه الله في القضاء والوقف. والفتوى على قوله فيما يتعلق بهما، وجوز للقاضي تلقين الشاهد وجوز كتاب القاضي إلى القاضي من غير سفر ولم يشترط فيه شيئًا مما شرطه الإمام، وصحح الوقف على النفس وعلى جهة تنقطع، ووقف المشاع ولم يشترط التسليم إلى المتولي ولا حكم
Similarly, the permissibility of exiting ihram in Hajj due to restraint (ihsar) and missing (fawat), and the permissibility according to Abu Yusuf (may Allah have mercy on him) of grazing the herbage of the Haram for a pilgrim during the season as ease, and wearing silk for itching and fighting, and selling a described item in the dhimmah like salam (advance payment) was permitted contrary to analogy to fulfill the need of the destitute, and sufficiency with seeing the visible part of a heap and a sample, and legislation of option (khiyar al-shart) for the buyer to prevent regret, and option of paying the price to prevent procrastination. Of this kind is the sale of trust (bay' al-amanah) called bay' ... by the scholars of Balkh and Bukhara as expansion, and its explanation is in Sharh al-Kanz from the chapter of khiyar al-shart. From that, the later jurists gave fatwa of return for the option of gross fraud (khiyar al-ghubn al-fahish), either absolutely or if there is deception, as mercy on the buyer.
Fulfillment (al-wafa'): And from it is the return due to defect, mutual oaths (tahlif), rescission (iqalah), transfer of debt (hawalah), pledge (rahn), guarantee (daman), release (ibra'), loan (qard), partnership (shirkah), compromise (sulh), interdiction (hajr), agency (wakalah), lease (ijarah), sharecropping (muzara'ah), and irrigation contract (musaqah), according to the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) with the fatwa given for need, and mudarabah, ariyah (loan of benefit), and wadi'ah (deposit), due to the great hardship that each one does not benefit except from what is his property, and does not receive except from the one upon whom his right is due, and does not take it except in full, and does not conduct his affairs except by himself. So the matter was eased by permitting benefit from another's property by way of lease, loan, and loan; and seeking assistance from another through agency, deposit, partnership, mudarabah, and musaqah; and taking from someone other than the debtor through hawalah; and securing the debt by pledge and surety, even by oneself; and dropping part of the debt through compromise or all through release, and for the need of redeeming his oath; we permitted compromise in case of denial, and due to the lack of that for which lease was legislated if benefits were made the rent when the type is the same, we said it is not permissible, and we said lease for a benefit not intended from the asset is not permissible due to dispensing with it through ariyah as known in the lease of bazaziyah.
And from the alleviations: the permissibility of non-binding contracts, because their binding would be difficult and thus cause them to be avoided, and the binding of binding contracts otherwise no sale or other would be stable, and we made the dismissal of an agent conditional upon his knowledge to prevent hardship upon him, and similarly the dismissal of a judge and the holder of his office.
And from it is the permissibility of breaking fast for a doctor and a witness, and during the sermon (khutbah), and for a master. And from it is the permissibility of marriage without seeing [the prospective spouse] because the hardship of requiring it, which many people cannot bear for their daughters and sisters—each suitor seeing—so ease was appropriate, so there is no option of seeing (khiyar al-ru'yah) in it, unlike sale, for it is valid before sight and has the option due to lack of hardship. Hence we said that the command is obligatory in marriage unlike sale, and hence Abu Hanifa (may Allah have mercy on him) was lenient and permitted it without a guardian and without requiring the justice of witnesses, and did not invalidate it by invalid conditions, and did not restrict it to the wording of nikah or tazwij, but said it is concluded by anything that indicates ownership of the object immediately, and validated it with the presence of the sons of the two contractors, drowsy and drunk persons who remember after sobriety, and by women's words, and permitted their testimony in it, so it is concluded in the presence of one man and two women, all that to prevent the hardship of adultery and its consequences. Hence it was said: 'I wonder at a Hanafi who commits adultery.' And from it is the permissibility of four wives; he did not restrict to one as ease for the man and also for women due to their abundance, and did not exceed four due to the hardship upon the man in division and other matters. And from it is the legislation of divorce due to the hardship of remaining in marriage when there is discord, and similarly legislation of khul', fidya, and return (raj'ah) in the waiting period before the third pronouncement, and it was not made perpetual due to the hardship upon the wife. And from it is the occurrence of divorce upon a husband who took an oath (moli) by the passage of four months to prevent harm upon her.
And from it is the legislation of expiation in zihar and oaths as ease for the obligated persons, and similarly the choice in expiation for an oath due to its frequency unlike other expiations due to their rarity, and the legislation of choice in a suspended vow with a condition not intended between the expiation of an oath and fulfilling the vowed act, according to what the fatwa is upon. And the Imam returned to it seven days before his death.
And from it is the legislation of kitabah (contract of manumission) so that the slave may be freed from continuous slavery due to the hardship in it, and it was not invalidated by invalid conditions as expansion.
And from it is the legislation of bequest at death so that one may make up for what he neglected during his life, and it is valid in one-third and not more to prevent harm to the heirs, so we permitted it with the whole when there is no heir, and we made it conditional upon the permission of the remaining heirs if it is for an heir, and we kept the estate on the deceased's ownership legally until his needs are fulfilled from it as mercy upon him, and we expanded the matter in bequest by permitting it for a non-existent [thing] and not invalidating it by invalid conditions.
And from it is the removal of sin from mujtahids in error and easing upon them by sufficing with probability; if they were required to take certainty, it would be difficult and hard to reach. And Abu Hanifa (may Allah have mercy on him) was lenient in the chapter of judgment and testimonies as ease; he validated the appointment of a corrupt person and said his corruption does not remove him [from office] but rather he deserves it, and he did not require the verification of witnesses' integrity as a solution for the state of Muslims as being virtuous, and did not accept abstract assault (jarh mujarrad) against a witness. And Abu Yusuf (may Allah have mercy on him) was lenient in judgment and endowment; the fatwa is upon his statement regarding them. He permitted the judge to prompt a witness, permitted the judge's letter to another judge without travel and did not require in it any of what the Imam required, validated a wqf upon oneself and upon a terminating destination, and validated a wqf of undivided property without requiring delivery to the trustee nor a ruling.
Source pages p. 68

Commentary
This passage is a detailed enumeration of Hanafi concessions derived from the overarching legal maxim 'hardship brings ease' (al-mashaqqah tajlib al-taysir). The author, likely Ibn Nujaym or a commentator on al-Ashbah wa al-Naza'ir, systematically lists applications across various chapters of fiqh. Each example illustrates how a ruling that would normally be based on strict analogy (qiyas) is relaxed due to hardship, need, or custom.

The passage begins with Hajj-related concessions: permitting exit from ihram due to restraint or missing the standing, and Abu Yusuf's opinion allowing grazing in the Haram for pilgrims. Then it moves to other concessions: wearing silk for medical or combat reasons, salam sales, option clauses, and the sale of trust (bay' al-amanah) as practiced by the scholars of Balkh and Bukhara. The 'option of gross fraud' (khiyar al-ghubn al-fahish) is mentioned as a later fatwa.

The central section discusses contracts like ijarah, ariyah, qard, wakalah, etc., which are normally based on strict property rights but are permitted due to the great hardship of doing everything oneself. The author explains the reasoning: ease is granted by allowing benefit from another's property through various contracts, and by allowing collection from third parties via hawalah, securing with pledge and surety, etc.

Further concessions: non-binding contracts (like wakalah, shirkah) are kept non-binding because binding would lead to avoidance; the dismissal of an agent requires knowledge to prevent hardship; judges and officials are treated similarly. Fasting is broken for a doctor, witness, during sermon, and master. Marriage is permitted without prior sight of the spouse (no option of sight), unlike sale, due to the hardship of requiring all suitors to see; Abu Hanifa went further by allowing marriage without guardian, without requiring witness justice, with imperfect wording, even with intoxicated parties, and with women's testimony, all to prevent the greater hardship of adultery. Polygyny is permitted up to four as ease, but not more due to hardship on the husband. Divorce, khul', and raj'ah are legislated due to hardship of staying in discord; a husband who swears to abstain (ila) is divorced automatically after four months to protect the wife.

Expiation (kaffarah) is legislated for zihar and oaths as ease, and choice in oath expiation is given due to frequency. Similar choice is given in suspended vows. Kitabah (manumission contract) is permitted to free the slave from perpetual servitude. Bequests are permitted to make up for missed acts, limited to one-third to protect heirs, but can be whole if no heir, and may be conditional upon heir's permission. Bequest for a non-existent thing (like building a mosque before construction) is allowed.

Finally, the passage addresses ijtihad: mujtahids are excused for error, sufficing with probability. In judiciary, Abu Hanifa allowed appointing a corrupt person and did not require witnesses' integrity to be verified; Abu Yusuf's leniency in judgment and waqf became the fatwa. He allowed the judge to prompt a witness, and the judge's letter to another judge without travel, and validated waqf on self and on a terminating category, and waqf of undivided property without delivery.

Throughout, the author emphasizes that these are all instances of the principle of easing hardship, and the Fatwa is often given on the more lenient opinion.

Key Terms
إجارة (ijarah): Lease contract for benefit of an asset in exchange for rent.
عارية (ariyah): Loan of a benefit without rent.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, on whose position is the fatwa given for most of these contracts?
A) Abu Hanifa only.
B) Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the two companions).
C) Imam Muhammad alone.
D) The later scholars of Balkh.

Key Takeaway
Many essential contracts are permitted as concessions from the default rule of ownership, based on the maxim of hardship.

Furuat al-Qawaid — Derived Applications
intermediate
8 min
Concessions in Marriage and Family Law
Concessions in marriage and divorce based on the maxim

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain how the maxim 'hardship brings ease' justifies lenient rules in marriage, including lack of sight, absence of guardian, and polygyny, as well as divorce and khul'.

Core Idea
To prevent the greater hardship of adultery and discord, marriage rules are eased.

This lesson covers concessions in nikah and talaq. The passage explains why marriage is valid without prior sight, without a guardian, with corrupt witnesses, and even with intoxicated parties. Divorce and khul' are legislated to release parties from harmful marriages. Polygyny up to four is allowed as ease for men and women.

Guided Path
1
Note the normal default for marriage
In principle, marriage requires sight of spouse, guardian, just witnesses, etc.
2
Identify the concessions
Abu Hanifa allowed marriage without sight, without guardian, with corrupt witnesses, etc.
These are leniencies.
3
Understand the reasoning
The text says all this is to prevent the hardship of adultery ('دفعا لمشقة الزنا').
The greater evil is avoided.
4
Apply to divorce and polygyny
Divorce allows exit from a harmful marriage; polygyny up to four eases both men and women.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كذلك، وإباحة التحليل من الحج بالإحصار والفوات وإباحة أبي يوسف رحمه الله رعي حشيش الحرم للحاج في الموسم تيسيرًا، ولبس الحرير للحكة والقتال وبيع الموصوف في الذمة كالسلم جوز على خلاف القياس دفعا لحاجة المفاليس والاكتفاء برؤية طاهر الصبرة والأنموذج ومشروعية خيار الشرط للمشتري دفعا للندم وخيار نقد الثمن دفعًا للمماطلة. ومن هذا القبيل بيع الأمانة المسمى ببيع جوزه مشایخ بلخ وبخارى توسعة وبيانه في شرح الكنز من باب خيار الشرط. ومن ذلك أفتى المتأخرون بالرد لخيار الغبن الفاحش ؛ إما مطلقا أو إذا كان فيه غرور رحمة على المشتري.
الوفاء ؛
ومنه الرد بالعيب والتحالف والإقالة والحوالة والرهن والضمان والإبراء والقرض والشركة والصلح والحجر والوكالة والإجارة والمزارعة والمساقاة، على قولهما المفتى به للحاجة، والمضاربة والعارية والوديعة، للمشقة العظيمة في أن كل واحد لا ينتفع إلا بما هو ملكه ولا يستوفي إلا ممَّن عليه حقه ولا يأخذه إلا بكماله، ولا يتعاطى أموره إلا بنفسه فسهل الأمر بإباحة الانتفاع بملك الغير بطريق الإجارة والإعارة والقرض وبالاستعانة بالغير وكالة وإبداعًا وشركة ومضاربة ومساقاة، وبالاستيفاء من غير المديون حوالة وبالتوثيق على الدين برهن وكفيل، ولو بالنفس وبإسقاط بعض الدين صلحا أو كله إبراء ولحاجة افتداء يمينه ؛ جوزنا الصلح عن إنكار ولفقد ما شرعت الإجارة له لو جعلت المنافع أُجرة عند اتحاد الجنس قلنا لا يجوز، وقلنا الإجارة على منفعة غير مقصودة من العين لا تجوز للاستغناء عنها بالعارية كما علم في إجارة البزازية.
،
ومن التخفيف جواز العقود الجائزة، لأن لزومها شاق فتكون سببًا لعدم تعاطيها، ولزوم اللازمة وإلا لم يستقر بيع ولا غيره ووقفنا عزل الوكيل على علمه دفعًا للحرج عنه، وكذا عزل القاضي وصاحب وظيفته.
ومنه إباحة الفطر للطبيب والشاهد، وعند الخطبة وللسيد. ومنه جواز النكاح من غير نظر لما في اشتراطه من المشقة التي لا يتحملها كثير من الناس في بناتهم وأخواتهم ؛ من نظر كل خاطب فناسب التيسير فلم يكن فيه خيار رؤية بخلاف البيع فإنه يصح قبل الرؤية وله الخيار لعدم المشقة، ومن ثم قلنا إن الأمر إيجاب في النكاح بخلاف البيع، ومن هنا وسع فيه أبو حنيفة رحمه الله فجوَّزه بلا ولي ومن غير اشتراط عدالة الشهود، ولم يفسده بالشروط المفسدة، ولم يخصه بلفظ النكاح والتزويج بل قال ينعقد بما يفيد ملك العين للحال، وصححه بحضور ابني العاقدين وناعسين وسكارى يذكرونه بعد الصحو، وبعبارة النساء، وجوّز شهادتهنَّ فيه، فانعقد بحضرة رجل وامرأتين كل ذلك دفعا لمشقة الزنا وما يترتب عليه. ومن هنا قيل عجبت لحنفي يزني. ومنه إباحة أربع نسوة؛ فلم يقتصر على واحدة تيسيرًا على الرجل وعلى النساء أيضًا لكثرتهنَّ، ولم يزد على أربعة لما فيه من المشقة على الرجل في القسم وغيره. ومنه مشروعية الطلاق لما في البقاء على الزوجية من المشقة عند التنافر، وكذا مشروعية الخلع والافتداء والرجعة في العدة قبل الثلاث، ولم يشرع دائما لما فيه من المشقة على الزوجة . ومنه وقوع الطلاق على المولى بمضي أربعة أشهر دفعا للضرر عنها.
ومنه مشروعية الكفَّارة في الظهار واليمين تيسيرًا على المكلفين، وكذا التخيير في كفَّارة اليمين لتكررها بخلاف بقية الكفَّارات لندرة وقوعها، ومشروعية التخيير في نذر معلق بشرط لا يُراد كونه بين كفَّارة اليمين والوفاء بالمنذور على ما عليه الفتوى. وإليه رجع الإمام قبل موته بسبعة أيام.
ومنه مشروعية الكتابة ليتخلص العبد من دوام الرقّ لما فيه من العسر، ولم يبطلها بالشروط الفاسدة توسعة.
ومنه مشروعية الوصية عند الموت ليتدارك الإنسان ما فرط منه في حال حياته وصح له في الثلث دون ما زاد عليه دفعًا لضرر الورثة حتى أجزناها بالجميع عند عدم الوارث، وأوقفناها على إجازة بقية الورثة إذا كانت لوارث وأبقينا التركة على ملك الميت حكمًا حتى تقضى حوائجه منها رحمة عليه، ووسعنا الأمر في الوصية فجوزناها بالمعدوم ولم نبطلها بالشروط الفاسدة.
·
ومنه إسقاط الإثم عن المجتهدين في الخطأ والتيسير عليهم بالاكتفاء بالظن ولو كلفوا الأخذ باليقين لشقّ وعسر الوصول إليه، ووسع أبو حنيفة رحمه الله في باب القضاء والشهادات تيسيرًا؛ فصحح تولية الفاسق وقال إن فسقه لا يعزله وإنما يستحقه، ولم يوجب تزكية الشهود حلاً لحال المسلمين على الصلاح، ولم يقبل الجرح المجرَّد في الشاهد ووسع أبو يوسف رحمه الله في القضاء والوقف. والفتوى على قوله فيما يتعلق بهما، وجوز للقاضي تلقين الشاهد وجوز كتاب القاضي إلى القاضي من غير سفر ولم يشترط فيه شيئًا مما شرطه الإمام، وصحح الوقف على النفس وعلى جهة تنقطع، ووقف المشاع ولم يشترط التسليم إلى المتولي ولا حكم

And the Imam returned to it seven days before his death.
And from it is the legislation of kitabah (contract of manumission) so that the slave may be freed from continuous slavery due to the hardship in it, and it was not invalidated by invalid conditions as expansion.
And from it is the legislation of bequest at death so that one may make up for what he neglected during his life, and it is valid in one-third and not more to prevent harm to the heirs, so we permitted it with the whole when there is no heir, and we made it conditional upon the permission of the remaining heirs if it is for an heir, and we kept the estate on the deceased's ownership legally until his needs are fulfilled from it as mercy upon him, and we expanded the matter in bequest by permitting it for a non-existent [thing] and not invalidating it by invalid conditions.
And from it is the removal of sin from mujtahids in error and easing upon them by sufficing with probability; if they were required to take certainty, it would be difficult and hard to reach. And Abu Hanifa (may Allah have mercy on him) was lenient in the chapter of judgment and testimonies as ease; he validated the appointment of a corrupt person and said his corruption does not remove him [from office] but rather he deserves it, and he did not require the verification of witnesses' integrity as a solution for the state of Muslims as being virtuous, and did not accept abstract assault (jarh mujarrad) against a witness. And Abu Yusuf (may Allah have mercy on him) was lenient in judgment and endowment; the fatwa is upon his statement regarding them. He permitted the judge to prompt a witness, permitted the judge's letter to another judge without travel and did not require in it any of what the Imam required, validated a wqf upon oneself and upon a terminating destination, and validated a wqf of undivided property without requiring delivery to the trustee nor a ruling.
Source pages p. 68

Commentary
This passage is a detailed enumeration of Hanafi concessions derived from the overarching legal maxim 'hardship brings ease' (al-mashaqqah tajlib al-taysir). The author, likely Ibn Nujaym or a commentator on al-Ashbah wa al-Naza'ir, systematically lists applications across various chapters of fiqh. Each example illustrates how a ruling that would normally be based on strict analogy (qiyas) is relaxed due to hardship, need, or custom.

The passage begins with Hajj-related concessions: permitting exit from ihram due to restraint or missing the standing, and Abu Yusuf's opinion allowing grazing in the Haram for pilgrims. Then it moves to other concessions: wearing silk for medical or combat reasons, salam sales, option clauses, and the sale of trust (bay' al-amanah) as practiced by the scholars of Balkh and Bukhara. The 'option of gross fraud' (khiyar al-ghubn al-fahish) is mentioned as a later fatwa.

The central section discusses contracts like ijarah, ariyah, qard, wakalah, etc., which are normally based on strict property rights but are permitted due to the great hardship of doing everything oneself. The author explains the reasoning: ease is granted by allowing benefit from another's property through various contracts, and by allowing collection from third parties via hawalah, securing with pledge and surety, etc.

Further concessions: non-binding contracts (like wakalah, shirkah) are kept non-binding because binding would lead to avoidance; the dismissal of an agent requires knowledge to prevent hardship; judges and officials are treated similarly. Fasting is broken for a doctor, witness, during sermon, and master. Marriage is permitted without prior sight of the spouse (no option of sight), unlike sale, due to the hardship of requiring all suitors to see; Abu Hanifa went further by allowing marriage without guardian, without requiring witness justice, with imperfect wording, even with intoxicated parties, and with women's testimony, all to prevent the greater hardship of adultery. Polygyny is permitted up to four as ease, but not more due to hardship on the husband. Divorce, khul', and raj'ah are legislated due to hardship of staying in discord; a husband who swears to abstain (ila) is divorced automatically after four months to protect the wife.

Expiation (kaffarah) is legislated for zihar and oaths as ease, and choice in oath expiation is given due to frequency. Similar choice is given in suspended vows. Kitabah (manumission contract) is permitted to free the slave from perpetual servitude. Bequests are permitted to make up for missed acts, limited to one-third to protect heirs, but can be whole if no heir, and may be conditional upon heir's permission. Bequest for a non-existent thing (like building a mosque before construction) is allowed.

Finally, the passage addresses ijtihad: mujtahids are excused for error, sufficing with probability. In judiciary, Abu Hanifa allowed appointing a corrupt person and did not require witnesses' integrity to be verified; Abu Yusuf's leniency in judgment and waqf became the fatwa. He allowed the judge to prompt a witness, and the judge's letter to another judge without travel, and validated waqf on self and on a terminating category, and waqf of undivided property without delivery.

Throughout, the author emphasizes that these are all instances of the principle of easing hardship, and the Fatwa is often given on the more lenient opinion.

Key Terms
خيار الرؤية (khiyar al-ru'yah): Option to rescind a contract after seeing the object; not present in marriage.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why did Abu Hanifa permit marriage without requiring the justice of witnesses?
A) Because justice is impossible to ascertain.
B) To prevent the hardship of adultery.
C) Because the Quran does not mention witness justice.
D) To encourage polygyny.

Key Takeaway
Abu Hanifa's lenient rulings on marriage are driven by the maxim to prevent the greater hardship of adultery.

Furuat al-Qawaid — Derived Applications
intermediate

Concessions in Judiciary, Ijtihad, and Waqf
Concessions in judiciary, ijtihad, and waqf

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the maxim 'hardship brings ease' to justify lenient rules in judiciary (appointing a corrupt judge, not requiring witness verification) and ijtihad (sufficing with probability), and in waqf (validating waqf on oneself).

Core Idea
Sufficing with probability and leniency in judiciary ease the burden of certainty.

The passage concludes with concessions in the sphere of judiciary and ijtihad. Abu Hanifa allowed appointing a corrupt judge and did not require verification of witnesses' integrity, assuming Muslims are virtuous unless proven otherwise. In ijtihad, sufficing with probability (zann) is sufficient, not certainty. Abu Yusuf's leniency in waqf and judicial matters became the fatwa.

Guided Path
1
Identify the default strict rule
Ideally, a judge must be just, witnesses must be verified, ijtihad requires certainty.
2
Note the concessions
Appointing a fasiq judge is valid; witnesses are assumed just; mujtahid excused for error; waqf on self validated.
3
Understand the reasoning
Requiring absolute justice would bring affairs to a standstill; sufficing with probability eases the burden.
4
Note the mufta bihi positions
Abu Yusuf's positions on waqf and judiciary are relied upon.

كذلك، وإباحة التحليل من الحج بالإحصار والفوات وإباحة أبي يوسف رحمه الله رعي حشيش الحرم للحاج في الموسم تيسيرًا، ولبس الحرير للحكة والقتال وبيع الموصوف في الذمة كالسلم جوز على خلاف القياس دفعا لحاجة المفاليس والاكتفاء برؤية طاهر الصبرة والأنموذج ومشروعية خيار الشرط للمشتري دفعا للندم وخيار نقد الثمن دفعًا للمماطلة. ومن هذا القبيل بيع الأمانة المسمى ببيع جوزه مشایخ بلخ وبخارى توسعة وبيانه في شرح الكنز من باب خيار الشرط. ومن ذلك أفتى المتأخرون بالرد لخيار الغبن الفاحش ؛ إما مطلقا أو إذا كان فيه غرور رحمة على المشتري.
الوفاء ؛
ومنه الرد بالعيب والتحالف والإقالة والحوالة والرهن والضمان والإبراء والقرض والشركة والصلح والحجر والوكالة والإجارة والمزارعة والمساقاة، على قولهما المفتى به للحاجة، والمضاربة والعارية والوديعة، للمشقة العظيمة في أن كل واحد لا ينتفع إلا بما هو ملكه ولا يستوفي إلا ممَّن عليه حقه ولا يأخذه إلا بكماله، ولا يتعاطى أموره إلا بنفسه فسهل الأمر بإباحة الانتفاع بملك الغير بطريق الإجارة والإعارة والقرض وبالاستعانة بالغير وكالة وإبداعًا وشركة ومضاربة ومساقاة، وبالاستيفاء من غير المديون حوالة وبالتوثيق على الدين برهن وكفيل، ولو بالنفس وبإسقاط بعض الدين صلحا أو كله إبراء ولحاجة افتداء يمينه ؛ جوزنا الصلح عن إنكار ولفقد ما شرعت الإجارة له لو جعلت المنافع أُجرة عند اتحاد الجنس قلنا لا يجوز، وقلنا الإجارة على منفعة غير مقصودة من العين لا تجوز للاستغناء عنها بالعارية كما علم في إجارة البزازية.
،
ومن التخفيف جواز العقود الجائزة، لأن لزومها شاق فتكون سببًا لعدم تعاطيها، ولزوم اللازمة وإلا لم يستقر بيع ولا غيره ووقفنا عزل الوكيل على علمه دفعًا للحرج عنه، وكذا عزل القاضي وصاحب وظيفته.
ومنه إباحة الفطر للطبيب والشاهد، وعند الخطبة وللسيد. ومنه جواز النكاح من غير نظر لما في اشتراطه من المشقة التي لا يتحملها كثير من الناس في بناتهم وأخواتهم ؛ من نظر كل خاطب فناسب التيسير فلم يكن فيه خيار رؤية بخلاف البيع فإنه يصح قبل الرؤية وله الخيار لعدم المشقة، ومن ثم قلنا إن الأمر إيجاب في النكاح بخلاف البيع، ومن هنا وسع فيه أبو حنيفة رحمه الله فجوَّزه بلا ولي ومن غير اشتراط عدالة الشهود، ولم يفسده بالشروط المفسدة، ولم يخصه بلفظ النكاح والتزويج بل قال ينعقد بما يفيد ملك العين للحال، وصححه بحضور ابني العاقدين وناعسين وسكارى يذكرونه بعد الصحو، وبعبارة النساء، وجوّز شهادتهنَّ فيه، فانعقد بحضرة رجل وامرأتين كل ذلك دفعا لمشقة الزنا وما يترتب عليه. ومن هنا قيل عجبت لحنفي يزني. ومنه إباحة أربع نسوة؛ فلم يقتصر على واحدة تيسيرًا على الرجل وعلى النساء أيضًا لكثرتهنَّ، ولم يزد على أربعة لما فيه من المشقة على الرجل في القسم وغيره. ومنه مشروعية الطلاق لما في البقاء على الزوجية من المشقة عند التنافر، وكذا مشروعية الخلع والافتداء والرجعة في العدة قبل الثلاث، ولم يشرع دائما لما فيه من المشقة على الزوجة . ومنه وقوع الطلاق على المولى بمضي أربعة أشهر دفعا للضرر عنها.
ومنه مشروعية الكفَّارة في الظهار واليمين تيسيرًا على المكلفين، وكذا التخيير في كفَّارة اليمين لتكررها بخلاف بقية الكفَّارات لندرة وقوعها، ومشروعية التخيير في نذر معلق بشرط لا يُراد كونه بين كفَّارة اليمين والوفاء بالمنذور على ما عليه الفتوى. وإليه رجع الإمام قبل موته بسبعة أيام.
ومنه مشروعية الكتابة ليتخلص العبد من دوام الرقّ لما فيه من العسر، ولم يبطلها بالشروط الفاسدة توسعة.
ومنه مشروعية الوصية عند الموت ليتدارك الإنسان ما فرط منه في حال حياته وصح له في الثلث دون ما زاد عليه دفعًا لضرر الورثة حتى أجزناها بالجميع عند عدم الوارث، وأوقفناها على إجازة بقية الورثة إذا كانت لوارث وأبقينا التركة على ملك الميت حكمًا حتى تقضى حوائجه منها رحمة عليه، ووسعنا الأمر في الوصية فجوزناها بالمعدوم ولم نبطلها بالشروط الفاسدة.
·
ومنه إسقاط الإثم عن المجتهدين في الخطأ والتيسير عليهم بالاكتفاء بالظن ولو كلفوا الأخذ باليقين لشقّ وعسر الوصول إليه، ووسع أبو حنيفة رحمه الله في باب القضاء والشهادات تيسيرًا؛ فصحح تولية الفاسق وقال إن فسقه لا يعزله وإنما يستحقه، ولم يوجب تزكية الشهود حلاً لحال المسلمين على الصلاح، ولم يقبل الجرح المجرَّد في الشاهد ووسع أبو يوسف رحمه الله في القضاء والوقف. والفتوى على قوله فيما يتعلق بهما، وجوز للقاضي تلقين الشاهد وجوز كتاب القاضي إلى القاضي من غير سفر ولم يشترط فيه شيئًا مما شرطه الإمام، وصحح الوقف على النفس وعلى جهة تنقطع، ووقف المشاع ولم يشترط التسليم إلى المتولي ولا حكم
Similarly, the permissibility of exiting ihram in Hajj due to restraint (ihsar) and missing (fawat), and the permissibility according to Abu Yusuf (may Allah have mercy on him) of grazing the herbage of the Haram for a pilgrim during the season as ease, and wearing silk for itching and fighting, and selling a described item in the dhimmah like salam (advance payment) was permitted contrary to analogy to fulfill the need of the destitute, and sufficiency with seeing the visible part of a heap and a sample, and legislation of option (khiyar al-shart) for the buyer to prevent regret, and option of paying the price to prevent procrastination. Of this kind is the sale of trust (bay' al-amanah) called bay' ... by the scholars of Balkh and Bukhara as expansion, and its explanation is in Sharh al-Kanz from the chapter of khiyar al-shart. From that, the later jurists gave fatwa of return for the option of gross fraud (khiyar al-ghubn al-fahish), either absolutely or if there is deception, as mercy on the buyer.
Fulfillment (al-wafa'): And from it is the return due to defect, mutual oaths (tahlif), rescission (iqalah), transfer of debt (hawalah), pledge (rahn), guarantee (daman), release (ibra'), loan (qard), partnership (shirkah), compromise (sulh), interdiction (hajr), agency (wakalah), lease (ijarah), sharecropping (muzara'ah), and irrigation contract (musaqah), according to the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) with the fatwa given for need, and mudarabah, ariyah (loan of benefit), and wadi'ah (deposit), due to the great hardship that each one does not benefit except from what is his property, and does not receive except from the one upon whom his right is due, and does not take it except in full, and does not conduct his affairs except by himself. So the matter was eased by permitting benefit from another's property by way of lease, loan, and loan; and seeking assistance from another through agency, deposit, partnership, mudarabah, and musaqah; and taking from someone other than the debtor through hawalah; and securing the debt by pledge and surety, even by oneself; and dropping part of the debt through compromise or all through release, and for the need of redeeming his oath; we permitted compromise in case of denial, and due to the lack of that for which lease was legislated if benefits were made the rent when the type is the same, we said it is not permissible, and we said lease for a benefit not intended from the asset is not permissible due to dispensing with it through ariyah as known in the lease of bazaziyah.
And from the alleviations: the permissibility of non-binding contracts, because their binding would be difficult and thus cause them to be avoided, and the binding of binding contracts otherwise no sale or other would be stable, and we made the dismissal of an agent conditional upon his knowledge to prevent hardship upon him, and similarly the dismissal of a judge and the holder of his office.
And from it is the permissibility of breaking fast for a doctor and a witness, and during the sermon (khutbah), and for a master. And from it is the permissibility of marriage without seeing [the prospective spouse] because the hardship of requiring it, which many people cannot bear for their daughters and sisters—each suitor seeing—so ease was appropriate, so there is no option of seeing (khiyar al-ru'yah) in it, unlike sale, for it is valid before sight and has the option due to lack of hardship. Hence we said that the command is obligatory in marriage unlike sale, and hence Abu Hanifa (may Allah have mercy on him) was lenient and permitted it without a guardian and without requiring the justice of witnesses, and did not invalidate it by invalid conditions, and did not restrict it to the wording of nikah or tazwij, but said it is concluded by anything that indicates ownership of the object immediately, and validated it with the presence of the sons of the two contractors, drowsy and drunk persons who remember after sobriety, and by women's words, and permitted their testimony in it, so it is concluded in the presence of one man and two women, all that to prevent the hardship of adultery and its consequences. Hence it was said: 'I wonder at a Hanafi who commits adultery.' And from it is the permissibility of four wives; he did not restrict to one as ease for the man and also for women due to their abundance, and did not exceed four due to the hardship upon the man in division and other matters. And from it is the legislation of divorce due to the hardship of remaining in marriage when there is discord, and similarly legislation of khul', fidya, and return (raj'ah) in the waiting period before the third pronouncement, and it was not made perpetual due to the hardship upon the wife. And from it is the occurrence of divorce upon a husband who took an oath (moli) by the passage of four months to prevent harm upon her.
And from it is the legislation of expiation in zihar and oaths as ease for the obligated persons, and similarly the choice in expiation for an oath due to its frequency unlike other expiations due to their rarity, and the legislation of choice in a suspended vow with a condition not intended between the expiation of an oath and fulfilling the vowed act, according to what the fatwa is upon. And the Imam returned to it seven days before his death.
And from it is the legislation of kitabah (contract of manumission) so that the slave may be freed from continuous slavery due to the hardship in it, and it was not invalidated by invalid conditions as expansion.
And from it is the legislation of bequest at death so that one may make up for what he neglected during his life, and it is valid in one-third and not more to prevent harm to the heirs, so we permitted it with the whole when there is no heir, and we made it conditional upon the permission of the remaining heirs if it is for an heir, and we kept the estate on the deceased's ownership legally until his needs are fulfilled from it as mercy upon him, and we expanded the matter in bequest by permitting it for a non-existent [thing] and not invalidating it by invalid conditions.
And from it is the removal of sin from mujtahids in error and easing upon them by sufficing with probability; if they were required to take certainty, it would be difficult and hard to reach. And Abu Hanifa (may Allah have mercy on him) was lenient in the chapter of judgment and testimonies as ease; he validated the appointment of a corrupt person and said his corruption does not remove him [from office] but rather he deserves it, and he did not require the verification of witnesses' integrity as a solution for the state of Muslims as being virtuous, and did not accept abstract assault (jarh mujarrad) against a witness. And Abu Yusuf (may Allah have mercy on him) was lenient in judgment and endowment; the fatwa is upon his statement regarding them. He permitted the judge to prompt a witness, permitted the judge's letter to another judge without travel and did not require in it any of what the Imam required, validated a wqf upon oneself and upon a terminating destination, and validated a wqf of undivided property without requiring delivery to the trustee nor a ruling.

Furuat al-Qawaid — Derived Applications
intermediate
8 min
The Seventh Reason: Deficiency and the Two Types of Hardship
Explains the seventh reason for ease and divides hardship into inseparable and separable types.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to classify any given hardship as inseparable or separable and determine its legal effect on obligations using the maxim 'hardship brings ease'.

Core Idea
Deficiency and separable hardship are grounds for easing rulings; inseparable hardship is not.

The seventh reason for ease in the Hanafi legal maxims is deficiency (al-naqs), which encompasses states like minority, insanity, femininity, and slavery. This deficiency itself constitutes a type of hardship that justifies legal exemptions. The text then expands on the general principle of hardship by dividing it into two categories: inseparable hardships, which do not remove obligations, and separable hardships, which may, depending on severity, permit alleviation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the seventh reason and its examples
Read the opening section listing deficiency-based rulings: women exempt from Jumu'ah, jihad, jizya; children and insane under guardians; slaves half in hudud. Note that this deficiency is a kind of hardship triggering ease.
The key is that the deficiency itself, not an external difficulty, is the basis for exemption.
2
Distinguish inseparable vs separable hardship
The text divides hardship into two types: (1) Hardship that does not separate from the act usually (e.g., cold in wudu, heat in fasting, travel for hajj). (2) Hardship that separates from the act usually. The first has no effect on dropping obligations; the second can, if severe enough.
Inseparable hardships are inherent to the worship; they are part of the act's nature.
3
Understand the three ranks of separable hardship
Separable hardship is further divided into severe (e.g., fear for life), light (e.g., slight headache), and moderate (e.g., illness that may worsen). Severe necessitates alleviation, light is ignored, moderate permits it.
The text uses the example of a sick person in Ramadan: moderate sickness that risks increased illness or delayed recovery licenses breaking the fast.
4
Apply the classification to practical cases
Practice applying the rule: a person with a slight headache in Ramadan may not break fast (light hardship); a person with a fever that might worsen may break (moderate); a person facing a life-threatening storm during wudu in winter cannot abandon wudu if shelter is available (inseparable).
Note the special case of tayammum for janabah: severe cold is considered separable and permits tayammum only under strict conditions, but not for minor impurity.
5
Identify the tarjih in the passage
The text mentions a dispute about women bearing blood money (على قول والصحيح خلافه) and about the sick person's intention when fasting in Ramadan. Note which opinion is chosen as correct (الصحيح).
The mufta bihi is that women are not required to bear blood money, and a non-harmful sickness does not license breaking fast.

السبب السابع : النقص ؛ فإنه نوع من المشقة فناسب التخفيف؛ فمن ذلك تكليف الصبي والمجنون ففوَّض أمر أموالها إلى الولي وتربيته وحضانته إلى النساء رحمة عليه ولم يجبرهنَّ على الحضانة تيسيرًا عليهنَّ وعدم تكليف النساء بكثير مما وجب على الرجال ؛ كالجماعة والجمعة والجهاد والجزية وتحمّل العقل على قول . والصحيح خلافه، وإباحة لبس الحرير وحلي الذهب، وعدم تكليف الأرقاء بكثير مما وجب على الأحرار لكونه على النصف من الحرّ في الحدود والعدة مما سيأتي في أحكام العبيد. وهذه فوائد مهمة نختم بها الكلام على هذه القاعدة. الفائدة الأولى : المشاق على قسمين : مشقّة لا تنفك عنها العبادة غالبا ؛ كمشقة البرد في الوضوء والغسل ومشقة الصوم في شدَّة الحرّ وطول النهار، ومشقة السفر التي لا انفكاك للحج والجهاد عنها ومشقة ألم الحدّ ورجم الزناة وقتل الجناة وقتال البغاة، فلا أثر لها في إسقاط العبادات في كل الأوقات وأما جواز التيمم للخوف من شدة البرد للجنابة؛ فالمراد من الخوف الخوف من الاغتسال على نفسه أو على عضو من أعضائه أو من حصول مرض. ولذا اشترط في البدائع لجوازه من الجنابة أن لا يجد مكانا يأويه ولا ثوبا يتدفأ به ولا ماء مسخنا ولا حماما. والصحيح أنه لا يجوز للحدث الأصغر، كما في الخانية لعدم اعتبار ذلك الخوف في أعضاء الوضوء. وأما المشقة التي تنفك عنها العبادات غالبا فعلى مراتب : الأولى : مشقة عظيمة فادحة كمشقَّة الخوف على النفوس والأطراف ومنافع الأعضاء فهي موجبة المتخفيف وكذا إذا لم يكن للحج طريق إلا من البحر وكان الغالب عدم السلامة لم يجب. الثانية : مشقة خفيفة؛ كأدنى وجع في أصبع أو أدنى صداع في الرأس أو سوء مزاج خفيف فهذا لا أثر له ولا التفات إليه لأن تحصيل مصالح العبادات أولى من دفع مثل هذه المفسدة التي لا أثر لها. ومن هنا ردَّ على من قال من مشايخنا : إن المريض إذا نوى الصوم في رمضان عن واجب آخر ; فإنه يقع عما نوى إن كان مرضًا لا يضر معه الصوم، وإلا فيقع عن رمضان - بأن ما لا يضر ليس بمرخص للفطر في رمضان، وكلامنا في مريض رخص له الفطر. تنبيه : مرضها مطلق المرض وإن لم يضرّ ; إن كان بالزوج مانع من صحة خلوته بها بخلاف ( الثانية : متوسطة بين هاتين ; كمريض في رمضان يخاف من الصوم زيادة المرض أو بطء البرء فيجوز له الفطر، وهكذا في المرض المبيح للتيمم، واعتبروا في الحج الزاد والراحلة المناسبين للشخص حتى قال في فتح القدير : يعتبر في حق كل إنسان ما يصح معه بدنه وقالوا : لا يكتفي بالعقبة في الراحلة بل لا بد في الحج من شق محمل أو رأس زاملة ومن المشكل التيمّم ; فإنهم اشترطوا في المرض المبيح له أن من الماء على نفسه أو عضوه ذهابًا أو منفعة أو حدوث مرض أو بطء ولم يبيحوه بمطلق المرض مع أن مشقة السفر دون ذلك بكثير. ولم يوجبوا شراء الماء بزيادة فاحشة على قيمته لا اليسيرة.
The seventh reason: deficiency; for it is a kind of hardship, so ease is appropriate. Of that: the obligation upon the child and the insane – they delegated their wealth to the guardian and his upbringing and custody to women out of mercy, and they were not compelled to custody for their ease, and the non-obligation of women upon much that is obligatory upon men, like congregational prayer, Friday prayer, jihad, jizya, and bearing the blood money according to a saying; and the correct is otherwise. And the permissibility of wearing silk and gold ornaments, and the non-obligation of slaves upon much that is obligatory upon free persons because they are half of the free in hudud and iddah, as will come in the rulings of slaves. These are important benefits with which we conclude the discussion on this maxim. First benefit: Hardships are of two types: Hardship that does not separate from worship usually, like the hardship of cold in wudu and ghusl, the hardship of fasting in severe heat and long days, the hardship of travel that is inseparable from hajj and jihad, and the hardship of pain of hadd, stoning of adulterers, execution of criminals, and fighting rebels – these have no effect in dropping acts of worship at all times. As for the permissibility of tayammum due to fear of severe cold for janabah: the meaning of fear is fear of bathing harming himself or a limb or causing illness. Hence it was stipulated in al-Badai for its permissibility from janabah that he finds no shelter, no clothing to warm himself, no heated water, and no bathhouse. The correct view is that it is not permissible for minor impurity, as in al-Khaniyyah, because that fear is not considered for the limbs of wudu. As for hardship that separates from worship usually, it has ranks: First: great severe hardship, like fear for life, limbs, and organ functions – it necessitates alleviation. Similarly, if there is no way for hajj except by sea and safety is generally not assured, it is not obligatory. Second: light hardship, like a slight pain in a finger, slight headache, or light malaise – this has no effect and is not considered, because achieving the benefits of worship takes precedence over repelling such insignificant harm. Hence it was rejected from those of our scholars who said: If a sick person intends fasting in Ramadan for another obligation, it falls for what he intended if the sickness does not harm him with fasting; otherwise it falls for Ramadan – with the response that what does not harm is not a license to break fast in Ramadan, and our discussion concerns a sick person who is licensed to break fast. Warning: Her illness, absolute illness even if not harmful, if it is with the husband prevents the validity of his seclusion with her, unlike ( Second: medium between these two, like a sick person in Ramadan who fears increase of illness or delay of recovery from fasting – he may break his fast. Similarly for illness permitting tayammum. They considered in hajj the provisions and mount suitable for the person, so much so that it is said in Fath al-Qadir: It is considered for each person what his body can endure. And they said: One is not content with a mount that can only climb a mountain path, but there must be in hajj a saddle frame or a camel litter. And problematic is tayammum: for they stipulated in the illness permitting it that he fears from water on himself or his limb loss or harm or onset of illness or delay of recovery, and they did not permit it for absolute illness, even though the hardship of travel is far less than that. And they did not require buying water at an exorbitant increase over its value, only a slight one.
Source pages p. 70

Commentary
This passage is an expansion of the qawida 'Hardship brings ease' (المشقة تجلب التيسير). The author begins by listing the seventh reason for ease: deficiency (النقص). This refers to legal deficiency due to minority, insanity, femininity, or slavery. Examples include: children and the insane having their wealth managed by guardians; women being exempt from congregational prayer, Friday prayer, jihad, jizya, and (in one view) bearing blood money; permissibility of silk and gold for women; slaves being treated as half-free in certain penalties and waiting periods. These are applications of the maxim: the hardship of deficiency is lightened by reducing or removing obligations. Then the author presents the first of two important benefits: a detailed classification of hardships. Hardships are of two main types: (1) Inseparable hardship (لا تنفك عن العبادة غالبا) – e.g., cold in wudu, heat in fasting, travel for hajj, pain in hadd punishments. These have no effect on abrogating obligations because they are inherent to the acts. Tayammum for severe cold is only allowed for janabah (major impurity) under strict conditions, not for minor hadath. (2) Separable hardship (تنفك عن العبادات غالبا) – this has three ranks: (a) Severe hardship (مشقة عظيمة فادحة) – e.g., fear of life or limb, which obligates alleviation such as not requiring hajj if sea travel is dangerous. (b) Light hardship (مشقة خفيفة) – e.g., slight pain – ignored, as the benefits of worship outweigh trivial discomfort. The author refutes a view that a sick person with non-harmful sickness can intend a different fast in Ramadan; such sickness does not license breaking the fast. (c) Medium hardship (متوسطة) – e.g., sickness where fasting may increase illness or delay recovery; this licenses breaking the fast. For hajj, moderate hardship is considered in requiring adequate provisions and mount. A note clarifies that a wife's illness, even if not harmful, prevents valid seclusion. Finally, the author discusses the problematic case of tayammum: the scholars required specific harm from water, not mere illness, yet travel's hardship is much less but still permits tayammum. They also distinguished buying water: an excessive price is not required, but a moderate one is.

Key Terms
النقص (al-naqs): Legal deficiency due to minority, insanity, femininity, or slavery that reduces obligations or provides exemptions.
المشقة (al-mashaqqah): Difficulty or hardship that may or may not justify easing of legal rulings.
المشقة المنفكة (al-mashaqqah al-munfakkah): Hardship that can be separated from the act of worship typically, and can cause alleviation if severe enough.
المشقة اللازمة (al-mashaqqah al-lāzimah): Hardship that is inseparable from the act of worship, having no legal effect on dropping obligations.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which type of hardship justifies breaking the fast in Ramadan according to the passage?
A) Any headache, even slight
B) Hardship that is inseparable from fasting, like thirst in summer
C) Moderate hardship where fasting increases illness or delays recovery
D) Only life-threatening hardship

Key Takeaway
Deficiency is a distinct reason for ease; separable hardship requires severe or moderate degree to justify alleviation.

The Six Types of Legal Alleviations
Lists six types of legal alleviations with examples.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify all six types of takhfifat and apply each to a given fiqh scenario by matching the type to its definition and conditions.

Core Idea
Islamic law alleviates obligations through dropping, reducing, substituting, advancing, postponing, or permitting.

This passage from Al-Ashbah wa al-Naza'ir classifies the ways Islamic law eases obligations in cases of hardship. Understanding these six categories helps the mufti accurately determine which type of relief applies to a particular situation, ensuring that fatwa rulings are both precise and grounded in the grand maxim 'hardship brings ease.'

Guided Path
1
Identify the six categories
From the passage, list the six types: isqat, tanqis, ibdal, taqdim, ta'khir, tarkhis. Note their Arabic names and rough English equivalents.
Memorize the Arabic terms; they are standard in Hanafi usul al-iftaa.
2
Match each type with its definition
For each type, the passage gives a brief description. Focus on the core idea: dropping, reducing, substituting, advancing, postponing, permitting. Write a one-line definition in your own words.
Isqat = total removal; Tanqis = reduction in quantity; Ibdal = replacement; Taqdim/Ta'khir = time adjustment; Tarkhis = permission of a prohibited act.
3
Analyze the examples provided
The passage provides concrete fiqh examples for each type. For each example, confirm it matches the definition and note any conditions (e.g., tayammum requires inability to use water).
Note that the taqdim example for zakat requires owning the nisab; ta'khir for prayer is only for rescue situations.
4
Understand the internal Hanafi dispute on tanqis
The passage mentions two views on whether shortening prayer in travel (qasr) is a true reduction. Determine which view is mufta bihi and why.
The majority holds that completion (tamam) is original, so qasr is a reduction. A minority holds qasr as original, denying it as a true reduction.
5
Connect the types to the grand qawida
Relate each type to the maxim 'hardship brings ease' by asking: how does this type relieve hardship in the example given?
Each type operationalizes the maxim in a distinct way; the mufti must choose the appropriate type based on the form of hardship.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الفائدة الثانية : تخفيفات الشرع أنواع : الأول : تخفيف إسقاط كإسقاط العبادات عند وجود أعذارها . الثاني : تخفيف تنقيص : كالقصر في السفر على القول بأن الإتمام أصل. وأما على قول من قال القصر أصل والإتمام فرض بعده، فلا إلا صورة. الثالث: تخفيف إبدال كإبدال الوضوء والغسل بالتيمم، والقيام في الصلاة بالقعود والاضطجاع والركوع والسجود بالإيماء والصيام بالإطعام. الرابع تخفيف تقديم كالجمع بعرفات وتقديم الزكاة على الحول وزكاة الفطر في رمضان وقبله على الصحيح بعد تملك النصاب في الأول ووجود الرأس بصفة المؤنة والولاية في الثاني. الخامس : تخفيف تأخير كالجمع بمزدلفة، وتأخير رمضان للمريض والمسافر، وتأخير الصلاة عن وقتها في حق مشتغل بإنقاذ غريق ونحوه . السادس : تخفيف ترخيص كصلاة المستجمر مع بقية النجو، وشرب الخمر للغصة.
The second benefit: The alleviations of the law are types: First: Alleviation of dropping, like dropping acts of worship when their excuses exist. Second: Alleviation of reduction, like shortening prayer in travel according to the view that completion is the original. As for the view that shortening is original and completion is a subsequent obligation, then it is not [a reduction], except in form. Third: Alleviation of substitution, like substituting wudu and ghusl with tayammum, standing in prayer with sitting and lying down, bowing and prostration with gestures, and fasting with feeding. Fourth: Alleviation of advancement, like combining at Arafat, advancing zakat before the year, and zakat al-fitr in Ramadan and before it according to the correct view, after owning the nisab in the first and the existence of the head with the description of maintenance and guardianship in the second. Fifth: Alleviation of postponement, like combining at Muzdalifah, postponing Ramadan for the sick and traveler, and postponing prayer from its time for one occupied with rescuing a drowning person and the like. Sixth: Alleviation of permission, like the prayer of one who uses stones while some filth remains, and drinking wine for a choking person.
Source pages p. 71

Commentary
This passage presents the second benefit under the qawida of hardship bringing ease. It categorizes the types of alleviations (تخفيفات) that Islamic law employs to ease obligations in case of hardship. Six types are listed with examples: (1) Takhfif Isqat (dropping): complete removal of an obligation, e.g., dropping prayer, fasting, etc. when valid excuses exist like menstruation or travel. (2) Takhfif Tanqis (reduction): reducing the quantity, e.g., shortening the four-rakah prayers to two during travel, according to the view that completion (tamam) is the original. The other view (that qasr is original) does not consider it a true reduction. (3) Takhfif Ibdal (substitution): replacing the original act with something else, e.g., tayammum for wudu/ghusl, sitting/laying down for standing, gestures for bowing/prostration, and feeding the poor for fasting (fidya). (4) Takhfif Taqdim (advancement): performing an act before its due time, e.g., combining Zuhr and Asr at Arafah during Hajj, advancing zakat payment before the year-end, and paying zakat al-fitr before Eid (before Ramadan or during it) after possessing the nisab or having dependents. (5) Takhfif Ta'khir (postponement): delaying an act beyond its usual time, e.g., combining Maghrib and Isha at Muzdalifah, postponing Ramadan fasts for the sick/traveler, and delaying prayer for rescuing a drowning person. (6) Takhfif Tarkhis (permission/license): allowing something normally prohibited for necessity, e.g., the prayer of one who uses stones for istinja and still has some impurity (samaj: trace of stool) due to inability to clean fully, and drinking wine for a choking person when no other remedy exists. These examples show the comprehensive scope of the maxim 'Hardship brings ease'.

Key Terms
تخفيف إسقاط (takhfif isqat): Alleviation by dropping an obligation entirely due to a valid excuse.
تخفيف إبدال (takhfif ibdal): Alleviation by substituting one act with another permissible alternative.
تخفيف ترخيص (takhfif tarkhis): Alleviation by permitting normally prohibited things in cases of dire necessity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which type of alleviation allows a pregnant woman to break her fast and feed the poor?
A) Takhfif Isqat
B) Takhfif Tanqis
C) Takhfif Ibdal
D) Takhfif Tarkhis

Key Takeaway
The six types of takhfif—isqat, tanqis, ibdal, taqdim, ta'khir, tarkhis—provide a precise taxonomy for applying the maxim 'hardship brings ease' in fatwa rulings.
